  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5035aefe-a9bb-45cf-90f9-35bc4f9b657c'
      });
    }

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/23033604-karla"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1376299870i/23033604._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/23033604-karla">Karla</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I consider these books to be in the same genre as Pratchett (comic fantasy), but it's a very different style of writing, and different plots as well. <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I consider these books to be in the same genre as Pratchett (comic fantasy), but it's a very different style of writing, and different plots as well. I thoroughly enjoy them both, and if you like one, I'd recommend the other. <br /><br />Be warned though - if you like this book and continue reading the series, IMO they go downhill significantly after about book 8 (I'm going from memory here, so it may be slightly earlier/later)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2395706448" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2395706448" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2395706448?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=humor-and-comedy">humor-and-comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2395706448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2680610278117405452">Solid entertainment with unused potential that could have made it a pearl of the comedy fantasy genre.<br/> <br/>But there are some problems: <br/>Redundancy in dialogues, similar running gags, very many dead horse tropes. <br/>The first person view is a mess, it could have been much better with different perspectives and funny one time use characters. Asprin has a hand for comedy, I imagine many openings and endings with secondary characters for quick laughs, all things not possible from this narrative point of vi</span>
  <span id="freeText2680610278117405452" style="display:none">Solid entertainment with unused potential that could have made it a pearl of the comedy fantasy genre.<br /> <br />But there are some problems: <br />Redundancy in dialogues, similar running gags, very many dead horse tropes. <br />The first person view is a mess, it could have been much better with different perspectives and funny one time use characters. Asprin has a hand for comedy, I imagine many openings and endings with secondary characters for quick laughs, all things not possible from this narrative point of view.<br />First, it takes far too much time to get started for the action, then the action is over without really much happening.<br />The humor doesn´t reach higher levels, it´s always based on scenery or superficial character traits, no deeper meaning, connotations, relation to a meta scenery. The positive aspect of this is that it is pure entertainment without any darkness.<br /> <br />It´s still a solid work and if it would have been the average stereotype fantasy novel I wouldn´t have criticized it so much, but there was the chance of a rare, really funny fantasy read and after the first half or something it gets a bit boring because there is no more new under the sun. It had such a great start but became repetitive and just average that it´s truly a mess.<br /> <br />Absolutely not sure about continuing this, it´s short, which is always fine, and all parts are solid 4 star ratings, but I don´t think that there is still much potential for development and suspense, especially because of the lack of other character perspectives. Maybe I´ll give the second part a chance, funny writing is so rare that I´ll possibly just consume it for the laughs and vivisecting the used tropes.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/MythAdventures">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2680610278117405452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1666365919?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1666365919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4675208301001713591"><i>“C'mon kid. Think a minute, even if it hurts.”</i><br/><br/>Skeeve <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465927489i/19417883.jpg' width='340' height='340' alt='Skeeve' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>used to be a magician apprentice until an assassin (who paid for the deed with his life right away) brought an untimely end to his master, but not before the latter summoned a demon.<br/><i>“The Demon curled its lips back, revealing a double row of needle-sharp teeth. I considered changing my chosen course of action; I considered fainting.”</i><br/>Now Skeeve was stuck with the said demon who seems to have a very nice friendly personality:<br/><i>“Are you going to sha</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4675208301001713591" style="display:none"><i>“C'mon kid. Think a minute, even if it hurts.”</i><br><br>Skeeve <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465927489i/19417883.jpg" width="340" height="340" alt="Skeeve" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>used to be a magician apprentice until an assassin (who paid for the deed with his life right away) brought an untimely end to his master, but not before the latter summoned a demon.<br><i>“The Demon curled its lips back, revealing a double row of needle-sharp teeth. I considered changing my chosen course of action; I considered fainting.”</i><br>Now Skeeve was stuck with the said demon who seems to have a very nice friendly personality:<br><i>“Are you going to shake my hand, or am I going to rip your heart out?”</i><br><br>To complicate things further the demon turned out to be quite different from what anybody would expect: in his case "Demon" stands for "Dimensional Traveler" and the guy's native dimension was called Perv, making Aazh one of his inhabitants, or Pervert (another hint about his nice personality). The two teamed up to deal with the powerful magician who hired the assassin. Their weapons? Skeeve's rudimentary magic skills and Aazh's ability to talk anybody's head off. Fun times are about to start - and they sure will.<br><br>This book is funny. It has everything a good humorous fantasy is supposed to have: great puns, amusing dialog, absurd laugh-out-loud situations, colorful and equally amusing characters. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465927611i/19417900.jpg" width="300" height="420" alt="Tananda" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sadly this series nowadays is mostly forgotten and the first name that comes up when people think of humorous fantasy is Discworld. However it took Sir Terry Pratchett at least 3 books to become funny; this one makes you smile practically on the second page. The quality does drop off sharply after the first 5 or 6 books, but the initial ones are great. <br><br>My only complaint is that it took practically two thirds of the book before the dynamic duo arrived on Deva's Bazaar: a truly colorful place with some excellent recurring characters (see above). I can recommend this series to anybody who needs a good laugh; it also works great as a cure for a book hangover (my personal experience). </span>

          </span>

    <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner"><img alt="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551272804p2/3481302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2094322761?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2094322761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14824839129622576184"><i><b>"There are things on heaven and earth, Horatio, Man was not meant to know. "</b><br/>-HAMLET</i><br/><br/>Another Fine Myth follows Skeeve, who is apprenticed to a magician. This apprenticeship does not last long though as the magician is assassinated in the first few pages, coincidentally just after summoning a demon to show off the possibilities of magic to Skeeve. Needless to say, Skeeve is panicked as he has no idea how to control a demon, but the demon is not what he expects and pretty soon Skeeve finds himself o</span>
  <span id="freeText14824839129622576184" style="display:none"><i><b>"There are things on heaven and earth, Horatio, Man was not meant to know. "</b><br />-HAMLET</i><br /><br />Another Fine Myth follows Skeeve, who is apprenticed to a magician. This apprenticeship does not last long though as the magician is assassinated in the first few pages, coincidentally just after summoning a demon to show off the possibilities of magic to Skeeve. Needless to say, Skeeve is panicked as he has no idea how to control a demon, but the demon is not what he expects and pretty soon Skeeve finds himself on an unimaginable adventure with the demon, or dimensional traveller, who is named Aazh. No relation to Oz. Aazh is also a magician, but has been stripped of his powers, and so offers to teach Skeeve to better use his own budding abilities, doing them both a service and thus forming a new master / apprentice duo. What follows is an adventure that takes Skeeve to new dimensions and entertains throughout, with a regular doses of humour served up through fun banter, crazy characters, and unlikely situations.<br /><br />Lighthearted and amusing, Another Fine Myth is a quick, enjoyable read that is perfect material for that <i>not sure what to read</i> moment. If you are a fan of Terry Pratchett, you will most likely enjoy this one quite a bit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14824839129622576184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_270982073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270982073" />
    <a title="Stefan Yates" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates"><img alt="Stefan Yates" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328116275p2/7590340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270982073?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Yates" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Yates" href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates">Stefan Yates</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780441023615" href="/book/show/1785686.Another_Fine_Myth">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7590340-stefan-yates?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270982073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5291827591607285702">I read quite a few of the books in this series several years ago. I remembered enjoying it then, so I thought I'd give it a re-read now and see if the magik was still there. Indeed it is! Another Fine Myth is a highly entertaining light read that I couldn't put down.<br/><br/>The story revolves around the adventures of a young magician's apprentice, Skeeve. Skeeve is a likable character, if a bit naive and the misadventures that he gets into with his friends are a magical romp through a universe of magik,</span>
  <span id="freeText5291827591607285702" style="display:none">I read quite a few of the books in this series several years ago. I remembered enjoying it then, so I thought I'd give it a re-read now and see if the magik was still there. Indeed it is! Another Fine Myth is a highly entertaining light read that I couldn't put down.<br /><br />The story revolves around the adventures of a young magician's apprentice, Skeeve. Skeeve is a likable character, if a bit naive and the misadventures that he gets into with his friends are a magical romp through a universe of magik, demons, dragons and all sorts of other fantastical creatures. Because Asprin has incorporated different levels of technology in each dimension, there are really no limits on what might appear to challenge or aid our heroes. It's a lot of fun and always keeps you guessing as to what will happen next.<br /><br />Also, at only 200 pages, this book makes for a nice, quick break from other more weighty readings. I hope that I'm right in remembering that the rest of the series continues to be this enjoyable and I look forward to joining Skeeve and the gang again very soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5291827591607285702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1668613878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1668613878" />
    <a title="Orient" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43587353-orient"><img alt="Orient" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500791761p2/43587353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1668613878?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orient" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orient" href="/user/show/43587353-orient">Orient</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/30724281-another-fine-myth">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=desperado">desperado</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=killer">killer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=entertaining">entertaining</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=recs-by-evgeny">recs-by-evgeny</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1668613878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4340037844290066397">I read Evgeny’s great review about this book and decided that it's just perfect for me. Thanks, Evgeny, for turning my attention to this book ;) <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473105453i/20408693._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>The story in “Another Fine Myth” is filled with humor, puns and it is quick, easy, and a pure delight to read. I swallowed it in one day time enjoying each light-hearted and entertaining page (if not for my work it would have been quicker!). And I definitely had a laughable good time. It’s not a serious book with lot’s of depth, but it’s quick-paced an</span>
  <span id="freeText4340037844290066397" style="display:none">I read Evgeny’s great review about this book and decided that it's just perfect for me. Thanks, Evgeny, for turning my attention to this book ;) <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473105453i/20408693._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>The story in “Another Fine Myth” is filled with humor, puns and it is quick, easy, and a pure delight to read. I swallowed it in one day time enjoying each light-hearted and entertaining page (if not for my work it would have been quicker!). And I definitely had a laughable good time. It’s not a serious book with lot’s of depth, but it’s quick-paced and entertaining. Such things as death, serious feelings have no major attention and there isn’t much of character development but there are other books in the series (and quite a lot), so I really hope to know more about the main characters. There isn’t a character who overrules everyone, so I can't discern any of them, as the characters are different and they supplement each other. Though, book is more concentrated on the story than characters. But still I found fun and believable characters that made the book so entertaining for me. <br>An unskilled-skilled-to-be, naive and lazy apprentice with a baby dragon<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473105050i/20408633._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>a sarcastic Pervert (oops, sorry, a Pervect!!!) demon, made powerless by a practical joke<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473105050i/20408634._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> a beautiful, lustful, hot-tempered, green haired assassin <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473105050i/20408635._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>and other. I was happy to meet the green haired assassin as I enjoy rough-tough female characters and I hope to read about her more. <br>Each character comes alive and alluring with sarcastic/naïve comments, plays on words and the unexpected tricks. Also I liked that characters from other dimensions are presented as having certain qualities due to their home dimension. It’s a good start for other stories. <br>All in all, this book mixes fantasy, adventure, humor, and the facts of life into one awesome cocktail. The plot is quite simple, but unpredictability and wit made this book an enjoyable read to me.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4340037844290066397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1052307724" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1052307724?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1052307724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8210096733063181853">This was a lighthearted and humorous fantasy novel packed full of witty dialogue, action, and magic. I'm not a massive fan of books that have the main focus on humor, but I was pleasantly surprised by how much I laughed while reading this. It was a surprisingly enjoyable read. <br/><br/>Skeeve is an apprentice magician who's master is unfortunately assassinated while summoning a demon. Skeeve and the Demon are forced into an unlikely alliance with hilarious consequences and they flee the assassins and plo</span>
  <span id="freeText8210096733063181853" style="display:none">This was a lighthearted and humorous fantasy novel packed full of witty dialogue, action, and magic. I'm not a massive fan of books that have the main focus on humor, but I was pleasantly surprised by how much I laughed while reading this. It was a surprisingly enjoyable read. <br /><br />Skeeve is an apprentice magician who's master is unfortunately assassinated while summoning a demon. Skeeve and the Demon are forced into an unlikely alliance with hilarious consequences and they flee the assassins and plot to foil the plans of the mad wizard who hired them. <br /><br />The characters were likable and interesting. I loved the banter between Skeeve and Ahaz. The secondary characters were a diverse bunch who provided plenty of laughs. My favorite was probably the naive demon hunter Quigley, who was tricked by the quick witted Ahaz into all sorts of unfortunate mishaps. <br /><br />The world building was pretty good for such a short book. Skeeve's world of Klah is just one of many in a diverse universe. I'm eager to explore some of the others. <br /><br />Rating: 3.5 stars. <br /><br />Audio Note: Jeff Woodman gave an almost perfect performance. His character voices were well chosen and his sense of comic timing was excellent. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8210096733063181853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1185680413" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1185680413" />
    <a title="David Sarkies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies"><img alt="David Sarkies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470027282p2/5856247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1185680413?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sarkies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sarkies" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies">David Sarkies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780099627500" href="/book/show/1427138.Another_Fine_Myth">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like lighthearted fantasy</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to David by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/28247915-stewart-wymer">Stewart Wymer</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1185680413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3993608710119953668"><b>Adventure with a smart mouthed demon and his cheeky apprentice</b><br/>3 February 2015<br/><br/>	One of the main reasons that I read this book was because it kept on appearing on the Goodread's sidebar entitled 'Readers also enjoyed' which I suspect has something to do with all of the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett' title='Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Terry Pratchett</a> books that I have read. Okay, I generally don't pay all that much to Goodreads recommendations, but when I was much younger a friend of mine was really into the series and he had been trying to get me to read them as </span>
  <span id="freeText3993608710119953668" style="display:none"><b>Adventure with a smart mouthed demon and his cheeky apprentice</b><br />3 February 2015<br /><br />	One of the main reasons that I read this book was because it kept on appearing on the Goodread's sidebar entitled 'Readers also enjoyed' which I suspect has something to do with all of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a> books that I have read. Okay, I generally don't pay all that much to Goodreads recommendations, but when I was much younger a friend of mine was really into the series and he had been trying to get me to read them as well. Well, it has taken years but I finally (after being prompted by Goodreads) asked another friend, who also has the series, if I could borrow the first one – this one, and yes, I quite enjoyed it (though I am still not going to be blindly taking on Goodreads recommendations, especially with the number of books still on my shelf).<br /><br />	Okay, it's not Terry Pratchett, and while it is only the first book, the world itself didn't seem to be hugely developed, but it was still quite entertaining, and amusing. In fact, it seemed that the story was much more character driven and unlike Discworld, the world of Another Fine Myth, seems to sit quietly in the background allowing us to focus on some of the rather strange, and comical, encounters that the two main characters, Skeeve and Aahz, experience. <br /><br />	Basically Skeeve used to be a farmer, or was supposed to be a farmer, but instead decided to become a thief, and it seemed that that occupation didn't work out because he landed up as an apprentice to a magician. However, during one of his lessons, when the magician summons a demon, the magician is killed by an assassin which results in the demon (which actually means 'dimension traveller') being trapped on Skeeve's world. Adding the Aahz's problems is that Skeeve's master had stripped Aahz of his powers literally stranding him (otherwise he would have simply gone home). Then there is the assassination, which triggers a hunt for a magician that wants to take over the dimensions, as well as trying to escape from a couple of nasty imps that appear to be on their trail.<br /><br />	As I said, it is not satire in the vein of Terry Pratchett where the story pokes fun at modern society through the lens of a fantasy world, but rather a couple of larger than life cartoonish characters making their way through the adventure (though not necessarily stumbling because Aahz at least knows what he is doing and what is going on) poking fun at each other and those around them, and in a way outsmarting their enemies without actually drawing any blood (which also adds to the lighthearted aspect of this story). As I said, the characters are larger than life, such as Tananda, who regularly refers to Skeeve as 'handsome' even though she is leading a group of thugs to roll him, and the dragon Gleep (because all he says is 'gleep') who becomes attached to Skeeve because he nibbled on his shirt. Still, I've probably given way too much away already because this is one of those little gems that you should read knowing as little about it as possible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3993608710119953668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_30237864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30237864" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1385106-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217535570p2/1385106.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30237864?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/1385106-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30237864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7778432124450250164">One of my most childhood (well, teenagerhood) possessions is a pair of graphic novels based on Robert Asprin's "Myth" series, illustrated by Phil Foglio. I also read most of the books themselves and enjoyed them nearly as much. When I recently decided to re-read the first three books (Another Fine Myth, Myth Conceptions, and Myth Directions) I was surprised to find out how well they held up. They're still really fun!<br/><br/>Now while "fun" isn't the word I'd use to describe most books in the fantasy gen</span>
  <span id="freeText7778432124450250164" style="display:none">One of my most childhood (well, teenagerhood) possessions is a pair of graphic novels based on Robert Asprin's "Myth" series, illustrated by Phil Foglio. I also read most of the books themselves and enjoyed them nearly as much. When I recently decided to re-read the first three books (Another Fine Myth, Myth Conceptions, and Myth Directions) I was surprised to find out how well they held up. They're still really fun!<br /><br />Now while "fun" isn't the word I'd use to describe most books in the fantasy genre these days, these books certainly are. On the surface they're about a newly master-less magician's apprentice, Skeeve, who is mentored by a demon, Ahz, whose wisdom and experience are only matched by his panache for con jobs and profit. Each book is essentially a caper where Asprin weaves a huge cast of vivid characters into entertaining and often amusing situations. The author has a real gift for plotting to the point where even when the situations are outlandish and complicated, you can trace a clear line of how the characters got into them.<br /><br />And that's the point at which the real entertainment usually starts --when the characters have to get out of one mess and usually end up in another. What I like about these books is that Skeeve and Ahz and company don't win the day by being the strongest or the most powerful. They win it by using guile, trickery, improvisation, wits, and imagination. It's really satisfying to see these traits win out over seemingly impossible odds, and again Asprin has a gift for making it all believable within his own (admittedly self-created) rule set for the world he's constructed.<br /><br />It's also worth noting that the books are consistently upbeat and lighthearted, with minimal violence and only mild sexual inuendo. The humor is situational and character driven, but also makes extensive use of puns and pop culture references (though some of those are a bit dated at this point). I'd highly recommend them to people of just about any age. I plan on reading more of the series whenever I want to take a break between other books for something more refreshing and fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7778432124450250164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1523825373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1523825373" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1938544-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330120106p2/1938544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1523825373?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1938544-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780441023622" href="/book/show/1203856.Another_Fine_Myth">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Young adults, fantasy role-players, Asprin fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Michael by: </span>
      Seth Klein
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1938544-michael?shelf=literature">literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1938544-michael?shelf=satire">satire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1938544-michael?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1523825373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17354050872709833395">As it happens, I didn’t start reading this series with this book. Well, not exactly. I discovered “Myth Adventures” as a comic book drawn by Phil Foglio and read that, borrowing some issues from a friend and buying others. So, when I wanted to read the novels, I went looking for one called “Myth Adventures” to start with, but there wasn’t one. The title “Another Fine Myth” SOUNDED like a sequel, so I wound up starting with “Myth Conceptions” (number 2 in the series), and didn’t get back to readi</span>
  <span id="freeText17354050872709833395" style="display:none">As it happens, I didn’t start reading this series with this book. Well, not exactly. I discovered “Myth Adventures” as a comic book drawn by Phil Foglio and read that, borrowing some issues from a friend and buying others. So, when I wanted to read the novels, I went looking for one called “Myth Adventures” to start with, but there wasn’t one. The title “Another Fine Myth” SOUNDED like a sequel, so I wound up starting with “Myth Conceptions” (number 2 in the series), and didn’t get back to reading this one, I think, for several years. <br /><br />When I did, I was disappointed, actually. It’s not as good as the comic, for several reasons. First, it lacks the clever back-story for the major conflict and the inciting incident, which adds a lot of depth to the plot. Second, the hero in the book version is essentially a by-stander to the resolution, whereas in the comic, he’s directly responsible for it. Third, and perhaps most importantly, the cover art isn’t by Phil Foglio, meaning that it lacks his artistic renderings, especially of the assassin Tananda. Asprin also fixed a minor plot-hole at the beginning of the book in the comic, but that’s incidental.<br /><br />I usually try not to start by listing the flaws in a book, but in this case it seemed necessary to explain why I experienced this book differently than most of its readers. Still, for those who want to read the series, it is the starting point and does introduce many of the recurring characters as well as the inventive Universe that Robert Asprin built for them. Essentially, this is a comedy-adventure fantasy series in which a young apprentice magician teams up with a scaly-skinned Demon in order to learn magic (spelled “magik” throughout the series, which I refuse to do) and life’s lessons. A lot of the humor is verbal in some sense, and it tends to be somewhat low-key, compared to the non-stop laughs of Douglas Adams, for example. On the other hand, the adventure side tends to be better emphasized than in a lot of “funny” books, and there is genuine tension as the stories unfold, as well as good character development over time. You have to stick with the series to see that, however. <br /><br />Our hero is Skeeve, who starts out as a naïve young man on a medieval world apprenticed to a powerful wizard named Garkin. Garkin, trying to impress Skeeve, summons Aahz, the previously mentioned Demon, from his dimension just at the moment he is assassinated by (and simultaneously kills) an imp called Throckwaddle. Aahz, a dimension travelling resident of the world called Perv (“Demon” is short for “dimension traveler”), discovers that Garkin has stolen his magical powers as a practical joke, and thus he cannot return home for 100 years, so he takes on Skeeve as an apprentice and takes up the avenging Garkin’s death. In the meanwhile we also learn about the Deveels, residents of the dimension Deva, and their mighty bazaar, wherein anything in the Multiverse may be bought. They find a Deveel and arrange a trip there, along the way picking up a baby dragon called Gleep and the aforementioned assassin Tananda, who looks mostly human apart from having green hair. Oh, and there’s also a rather Dudley Dooright-like demon hunter named Quigley. And, of course, Isstvan, the mad wizard who sent the assassins out in the first place. <br /><br />As the series progressed, Asprin would fill in a great deal more details about the other dimensions and the monstrous beings who inhabit them (many are based on fantasy monsters of one kind or another), but he was just laying the groundwork here. What he does that appealed to me as a nerdy D&amp;D gamer, was to set out a believable yet simple system of magic and lead us progressively along the process of Skeeve’s training in that system. In that, the book does provide more satisfactory detail than the comics did, so reading it did ultimately pay off. Asprin was one of the first generation of fantasy writers who was also a gamer, so this makes sense. <br /><br />In general, though, if you’re just interested in the story, I’d recommend going over to <a href="http://www.airshipentertainment.com/mythcomic.php" rel="nofollow noopener">Myth Adventures</a> and reading the comics, now even in color, a benefit I didn’t have reading them in the 80s. Darn kids have it all too easy. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17354050872709833395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1806035675" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1806035675" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/291872-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1255380005p2/291872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1806035675?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/291872-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780441023615" href="/book/show/1785686.Another_Fine_Myth">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291872-thomas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291872-thomas?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291872-thomas?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291872-thomas?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1806035675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5362572484480711881">I'm not going to lie; reading this book is pure nostalgia for me. I first read the Myth books when I was fourteen or so, and I loved the heck out of them. I read and re-read them, and last year I saw that there are still books being published in the series. Asprin is dead, but another author has picked up the mantle. Honestly, I'm not interested in any of those, or any of the ones he co-wrote, but the idea of re-reading the series again, as an adult, made me giddy.<br/><br/>The book holds up remarkably we</span>
  <span id="freeText5362572484480711881" style="display:none">I'm not going to lie; reading this book is pure nostalgia for me. I first read the Myth books when I was fourteen or so, and I loved the heck out of them. I read and re-read them, and last year I saw that there are still books being published in the series. Asprin is dead, but another author has picked up the mantle. Honestly, I'm not interested in any of those, or any of the ones he co-wrote, but the idea of re-reading the series again, as an adult, made me giddy.<br /><br />The book holds up remarkably well. The plot is a bit thinner than I remember, but it's mostly exposition, anyway. Skeeve is a bumbling apprentice magician who is befriended by Aahz the Pervect after Aahz is summoned to Skeeve's dimension and stripped of his own powers. Gleep and Tanda are introduced along the way, and really, that's all that's necessary to get this story going. Asprin seemed to know at the time that he was writing a series, not just a single book, and spent the time laying the foundation of what was to come.<br /><br />The jokes aren't quite as funny as they were the first time, but how often are they? There was still a madcap feel to the story, and the banter between Aahz and Skeeve worked, and honestly, that was why I was reading the books. They're like old friends, and a large part of that is because the characters in the book are friends to each other. I was also pleased to see that Tanda is more than just a buxom maid trope; she's capable and independent and headstrong. I remember her that way, but I'm always a little concerned that stories of this age (almost 40 years!) carry some of the baggage of their eras. Another Fine Myth seems to avoid them.<br /><br />There are twelve books in the Myth Adventures series, and as much fun as I had with the first one, I expect to have fun with the rest of them, too. If nothing else, they're quick, short reads, and it shouldn't take long to plow through them. Right now, I think I need "fun" more than "thoughtful" anyway.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5362572484480711881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer354623016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14590014300550358270">I believe I was in about 6th or 7th grade when I first read Robert Asprin's "Another Fine Myth." I almost immediately blew through the other six books that had been published in the series by that point. I read the book once or twice more in the next couple years, but it had probably been close to twenty years since I last read it when I decided to give it another run through yesterday.<br/><br/>It holds up surprisingly well. I didn't find it as laugh-out-loud funny as I did when I was kid, but I was stil</span>
  <span id="freeText14590014300550358270" style="display:none">I believe I was in about 6th or 7th grade when I first read Robert Asprin's "Another Fine Myth." I almost immediately blew through the other six books that had been published in the series by that point. I read the book once or twice more in the next couple years, but it had probably been close to twenty years since I last read it when I decided to give it another run through yesterday.<br /><br />It holds up surprisingly well. I didn't find it as laugh-out-loud funny as I did when I was kid, but I was still amused and almost certainly had a greater appreciation of the light-hearted spoofs on the conventions of sword and sorcery genre.<br /><br />I'm sure that nostalgia colored my experience with this re-read, but even if this isn't one of your childhood favorites, it ought to be worth a try if you're looking for a fun, light read. Light, in this case, doesn't just refer to the tone, though. Fair warning -- this novel only runs to about 200 pages, which at today's paperback prices doesn't offer a lot of bang for your buck. I'd definitely suggest that you either look for a heavily discounted used copy or pick up the two-in-one that includes the second book in the series. The cost-per-page aside, the low page-count is probably a mark in the novel's favor, leaving no room for it to run out of steam. </span>

  <span id="freeText6900816497518311464" style="display:none">Short and fun! It's very much proto-Pratchett in its way of telling its story while affectionately mocking fantasy tropes with lots of humor. When a wizard summons a demon and gets murdered in the process, his apprentice is left to solve the murder with the help of said demon... who turns out to be an extradimensional lizard with the sardonic wit and canny intelligence of Sam Spade. Seems there's a Big Bad about who needs stopping, and our demon has a dozen tricky plans to do it. This twosome embarks on a quest through what's essentially a buddy movie fantasy adventure, filled with fast talking, sleight of hand, and plenty of comedic moments. <br /><br />The audiobook is just 6 hours long so it's a short bit of fun that never outstays its welcome. Recommended for fans of the Princess Bride, "The Fallible Fiend", and anyone who likes a dose of humor stirred into their swords and magic.</span>

<div id="review_315517454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/315517454" />
    <a title="So, I Read This Book Today" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8823926-so-i-read-this-book-today"><img alt="So, I Read This Book Today" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385785384p2/8823926.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/315517454?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="So, I Read This Book Today" class="user" itemprop="url" name="So, I Read This Book Today" href="/user/show/8823926-so-i-read-this-book-today">So, I Read This Book Today</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315517454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11459592767766016051">As a culture, we are always looking for the next best thing. Computers, cars, you name it. And, of course, books. Everything from urban fantasy to suspense, young adult to horror. Sometimes, though, what is New isn’t what we really need. Instead, what is Old is new again, or rather, it should be!<br/><br/>I just listened to Another Fine Myth by Robert Asprin, and narrated by Noah Michael Levine. First printed in 1978, I found the series way back then, and have the whole collection in paper. Recently, howe</span>
  <span id="freeText11459592767766016051" style="display:none">As a culture, we are always looking for the next best thing. Computers, cars, you name it. And, of course, books. Everything from urban fantasy to suspense, young adult to horror. Sometimes, though, what is New isn’t what we really need. Instead, what is Old is new again, or rather, it should be!<br /><br />I just listened to Another Fine Myth by Robert Asprin, and narrated by Noah Michael Levine. First printed in 1978, I found the series way back then, and have the whole collection in paper. Recently, however, the books have come out on Audible.com and, of course, I have to buy them all again. How can I help it? Noah Michael Levine does an amazing job of narrating! His voice and cadence are absolutely perfect for the reading. His grasp of accents is amazing, and he really brings the characters to life. I spent all night last night in my workroom, working on holiday gifts, and though I got really tired about 4AM, I couldn’t tear myself away. There is a sample reading on Audible, check it out and you will love it too!<br /><br />Why SHOULDN’T Robert Lynn Asprin’s Skeeve be the next Harry Potter?! It’s all there. Witches, Demons, and Wizards, Oh, My! And the Myth series is FUNNY. Like, burst out laughing on the airplane funny. And the voices by Noah take the laugh-out-loud character to a whole new level of laughter. Though Robert is now gone from us, his collaboration with Jody Lynn Nye means that the wonder of the tale lives on, and it is well worth the journey of discovery!<br /><br />Skeeve, the main character of the series, is an apprentice wizard. He doesn’t really care all that much about being an apprentice wizard, of course. He was previously a thief, who got busted by the Wizard he was trying to rob. Instead of turning him into a frog, or something just as icky, the Wizard makes Skeeve an apprentice wizard. What are ya gonna do?<br /><br />During the summoning of the Demon Aahz, an Assassin comes to call – and that is when things get rather messy. When the Wizard is killed, Skeeve is stuck now with the Demon Aahz, summoned from his own world, and none too happy about it. What follows? Well, you will just have to read the book to find out! Or rather, I would actually listen to it. You will NOT be disappointed if you like funny, well paced, creative and wonderful story lines.<br /><br />Enjoy!!!! Highly Recommended</span>
  <a data-text-id="11459592767766016051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1066870265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1066870265" />
    <a title="John Wiswell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/147818-john-wiswell"><img alt="John Wiswell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442531848p2/147818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1066870265?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Wiswell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Wiswell" href="/user/show/147818-john-wiswell">John Wiswell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780441023622" href="/book/show/1203856.Another_Fine_Myth">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1066870265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2952164332417737431">I recently had a conversation about how many movies are wish fulfillment about slacker everymen who are thrust into importance, causing everyone else in the world to put their lives on hold to assist their mission. And while I loved The LEGO Movie, <i>Another Fine Myth</i> is a fine alternative: it's the story of a slacker everyman who's roped into a demon's scheme and is dragged along, his life being put on hold for the antics of the journey. Our loser-boy is the aptly-named "Skeeve," and his teacher </span>
  <span id="freeText2952164332417737431" style="display:none">I recently had a conversation about how many movies are wish fulfillment about slacker everymen who are thrust into importance, causing everyone else in the world to put their lives on hold to assist their mission. And while I loved The LEGO Movie, <i>Another Fine Myth</i> is a fine alternative: it's the story of a slacker everyman who's roped into a demon's scheme and is dragged along, his life being put on hold for the antics of the journey. Our loser-boy is the aptly-named "Skeeve," and his teacher just summoned a demon before getting whacked by an assassin. The assassin went down as well, leaving the demon (the great and powerful "Aahz") stranded in the human world with no powers left. Skeeve, now without a magic teacher and employer, becomes Aahz's pupil, mostly learning to dupe people on a grand quest to regain the demon's powers and get him back home. Skeeve will have to survive some dire straits before he gets any respect (and, just like the modern slacker-hero, finding a girlfriend who's out of his league).<br /><br />It can be funny or cheesy, which is par for 70's/80's Fantasy humor, and it's something I wish I'd read when I was younger. Asprin's penchant for worldbuilding-via-funny-banter, and habit of resolving life-and-death conflicts with scumbag wheeling and dealing, is just fun and funny. I loved the demon trying to sell a crappy sword to a demon hunter under the pretense that the gems weren't garbage – they were so expensive they were *disguised* to look like garbage to protect them. Delightful as well is the Aahz's argument that he's only a demon in our dimension, and that if Skeeve were sucked into his dimension, everybody would be just as disgusted with him. A lot of this wit holds up.<br /><br />This is a short review for a short book, but Asprin also deserves credit for his brevity. At under 200 pages, <i>Another Fine Myth</i> never wears out its jokes, characters or quests. I've dropped too many books this year that ran out of creativity halfway through, whereas this novel, at less than half their length, wisely wraps itself up. If you want more, there are sequels. I'm going to check my library system for them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2952164332417737431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1824652783" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1824652783" />
    <a title="Michael Tildsley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2717220-michael-tildsley"><img alt="Michael Tildsley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442976905p2/2717220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1824652783?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Tildsley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Tildsley" href="/user/show/2717220-michael-tildsley">Michael Tildsley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1824652783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10463959302834506418">I had never heard of this author or this series before stumbling upon it at the library. I did not really have any expectations for it, which made what I found inside this book all the more delicious.<br/><br/>This series by Asprin is a Fantasy-Comedy series in the vein of Terry Pratchett, though not nearly as tongue-in-cheek or stuff-shirted as Pratchett can be. I love the guy, but only in small doses. Speaking of which, I finished this book in a single day. It was a fast, enjoyable read that was laugh o</span>
  <span id="freeText10463959302834506418" style="display:none">I had never heard of this author or this series before stumbling upon it at the library. I did not really have any expectations for it, which made what I found inside this book all the more delicious.<br /><br />This series by Asprin is a Fantasy-Comedy series in the vein of Terry Pratchett, though not nearly as tongue-in-cheek or stuff-shirted as Pratchett can be. I love the guy, but only in small doses. Speaking of which, I finished this book in a single day. It was a fast, enjoyable read that was laugh out loud funny at times. <br /><br />The plot itself wasn't anything to write home about really, and the climax and denouement are a bit hard to follow at first. Despite that, the book is an enjoyable read and a breath of fresh air from the things I have been reading and writing lately. I look forward to reading more of this series in the hope that Asprin keeps the laughs going, but maybe adds a bit more plot now that he has established characters.<br /><br />Briefly, I just wanted to add here that I cannot believe this book was first published in 1978. The writing style has a bit of a timeless quality to it. If you had told me it was written last year, I would have believed it. That's a pretty amazing feat for spec. fiction. The original Star Wars feels dated, but it only came out a year before this book. Pretty crazy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10463959302834506418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1694106203" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1694106203" />
    <a title="Anitha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41213075-anitha"><img alt="Anitha" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1694106203?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anitha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anitha" href="/user/show/41213075-anitha">Anitha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41213075-anitha?shelf=witty-fantasy">witty-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1694106203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15819135852838949381">Ready enjoyable witty fantasy, pure silly fun but with warmer characters than other satire I've read.<br/>The story begins with a poor thief turned apprentice magician Skeeve who meets a 'Pervert sorry Pervect' demon called Aahz, who was summoned to jazz up one of Skeeves's lessons. After the untimely demise of his own teacher Garkin, Skeeve becomes Aahz's apprentice and so begins their amusing adventure to avenge Garkin and set the world right. <br/>The only odd part of the whole narrative for me was the</span>
  <span id="freeText15819135852838949381" style="display:none">Ready enjoyable witty fantasy, pure silly fun but with warmer characters than other satire I've read.<br />The story begins with a poor thief turned apprentice magician Skeeve who meets a 'Pervert sorry Pervect' demon called Aahz, who was summoned to jazz up one of Skeeves's lessons. After the untimely demise of his own teacher Garkin, Skeeve becomes Aahz's apprentice and so begins their amusing adventure to avenge Garkin and set the world right. <br />The only odd part of the whole narrative for me was their actual confrontation of the baddie at the end, it was over in half a page with zero magical battles, I feel like I was missing something there. Nevertheless, I enjoyed everything else, so a solid 4 star from me, i'm looking forward to the rest of the series.<br /><br />Addition: Other reviewers who commented on the Pratchett similarity are entirely right, Asprin comes a close second in terms of satirical wordplay, role reversal of traditional characters and character-reader in-jokes (breaking the 4th wall?). He does not however use the sharp social commentary that is a beloved part of Pratchett's books, and in fact does not even try to. Keep this in mind if you are looking here for another discworldesque series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15819135852838949381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZUWsyLiRH5af7fWHEbRc1DqHRBTvzYY7BKNlMLjQv9TBEhTVM4ZkOqWUtsjwp7LHmGl85eAnkkqpzxHy074uJQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8K1zW5dZJ0py6kcYdZLQUu0uaZJeH6dfcIxFVPSb9gdU+stGHE5c5kiTBFeUgT5BT8BRY1H1sy7d4DGWn/Vn9g==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/65471.Robert_Lynn_Asprin">About Robert Lynn Asprin</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11734928023151172429">Robert (Lynn) Asprin was born in 1946. While he wrote some stand alone novels such as Cold Cash War, Tambu and The Bug Wars and also the Duncan and Mallory Illustrated stories, Bob is best known for his series fantasy, such as the Myth Adventures of Aahz and Skeeve, the Phule’s Company novels and the Time Scout novels written with Linda Evans. He also edited the groundbreaking Thieves’ World antho</span>
  <span id="freeText11734928023151172429" style="display:none">Robert (Lynn) Asprin was born in 1946. While he wrote some stand alone novels such as Cold Cash War, Tambu and The Bug Wars and also the Duncan and Mallory Illustrated stories, Bob is best known for his series fantasy, such as the Myth Adventures of Aahz and Skeeve, the Phule’s Company novels and the Time Scout novels written with Linda Evans. He also edited the groundbreaking Thieves’ World anthology series with Lynn Abbey. Other collaborations include License Invoked (set in the French Quarter of New Orleans) and several Myth Adventures novels, all written with Jody Lynn Nye.<br /><br />Bob’s final solo work was a contemporary fantasy series called Dragons, again set in New Orleans. <br /><br />Bob passed away suddenly on May 22, 2008. He is survived by his daughter and son, his mother and his sister.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11734928023151172429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
